## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science (solid mechanics, thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is characteristic of thermo-mechanical constitutive laws in materials science/solid mechanics. Common relationships include elastic (Hookean) response with temperature-dependent stiffness, thermal-expansion-induced stress offsets, and nonlinear/plastic hardening with thermal softening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity (temperature-dependent modulus): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness varies approximately linearly with temperature over a limited range)
- Polynomial modulus model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (smooth thermal softening/stiffening of elastic modulus)
- Exponential thermal softening of modulus: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (rapid reduction/increase of effective modulus with temperature; sign of c1 sets trend)
- Constrained thermal strain (thermal stress offset): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T + c2)) (stress driven by mechanical strain minus thermal expansion strain; c2 encodes a reference temperature)
- Nonlinear (Landau-type) thermoelasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**3 (captures symmetric elastic nonlinearity with thermal dependence)
- Ramberg–Osgood-type stress–strain with temperature-dependent compliance: epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (empirical elastic+nonlinear strain decomposition; invertible numerically to sigma(epsilon,T))
- Temperature-dependent hardening (power law): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (effective hardening exponent model; useful for monotone curves without explicit yield point)
- Thermally softened saturation stress (rational form): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon / (epsilon + c2) (stress saturates at large strain; temperature scales the saturation level)
- Elastic–plastic with smooth yield transition (tanh blend): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * tanh(c3 * epsilon) * exp(c4 * T) (adds a smooth yield-like shoulder with thermal softening)
- Johnson–Cook-like thermal softening (no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T)**c5 (strain hardening multiplied by a temperature softening factor expressed without explicit T* normalization)
- Piecewise elastic–plastic (yield strain as constant): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * Min(epsilon, c2) + (c3 + c4 * T) * Max(epsilon - c2, 0)**c5 (elastic up to yield strain then hardening; temperature affects both branches)
- Hyperelastic (1D neo-Hookean-like) with thermal shear modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon + c2) - (c3 + c4 * T) / (epsilon + c5) (captures strong nonlinearity at large deformation in a 1D surrogate form)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification: sigma proportional to epsilon (possibly with T-dependent slope) suggests Hookean elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus E(T).
- Thermal softening: decreasing slope d sigma / d epsilon with increasing T often implies multiplicative factors like exp(c*T) or polynomial E(T) multiplying epsilon.
- Thermal strain shifting: appearance of (epsilon - c*(T+c)) indicates stress driven by mechanical strain after subtracting thermal expansion, typical of constrained thermoelasticity.
- Nonlinear elasticity at moderate strain: odd-power terms (epsilon**3, epsilon**5) added to linear elasticity often represent anharmonic lattice response; coefficients may vary with T.
- Plastic-like saturation: rational forms epsilon/(epsilon+c) or bounded functions (tanh) indicate approach to a limiting flow stress or smooth yield transition.
- Hardening behavior: sigma increasing as epsilon**n (n>1) or via (c0 + c1*epsilon**n) indicates strain hardening; letting coefficients depend on T models thermal weakening/strengthening.
- Yield/transition behavior: piecewise or Min/Max structures correspond to an elastic branch followed by plastic hardening; T dependence in the breakpoint or slopes reflects reduced yield at high temperature.
- Coupled thermo-mechanical nonlinearity: terms like T*epsilon, T*epsilon**3, or exp(c*T)*epsilon**n suggest that temperature changes both stiffness and nonlinearity, not just an overall scale.

GT: c0*epsilon**c1 - c2*(T - c3) + epsilon**c4*c5*(T - c6)
Candidate formulas: 95

GT (fixed):
\[
4.2558304788\,\epsilon^3\;-\;0.3902956878\,(T-308.8646781)\;+\;8.6380281543\,\epsilon^3\,(T-308.8646781)
\]
Rewrite as an affine function of \(T\) with \(\epsilon\)-dependent slope/intercept:
\[
\text{GT} = \underbrace{\big(8.6380281543\,\epsilon^3 - 0.3902956878\big)}_{\text{slope in }T}\,T \;+\;\underbrace{\Big(4.2558304788\,\epsilon^3 + (0.3902956878-8.6380281543\,\epsilon^3)\,308.8646781\Big)}_{\text{intercept in }T}
\]
So GT is **linear in \(T\)**, and its \(T\)-slope is \(-0.3903 + 8.6380\,\epsilon^3\): i.e., it has a **constant term in the slope** plus an \(\epsilon^3\) term in the slope. Also, GT has **no \(\epsilon^2\), \(\epsilon^1\)** terms, and no non-polynomial dependence on \(T\) (no \(\sin,\cos,\exp,\log,\sqrt{T},T^p\) with \(p\neq 1\), no rational-in-\(\epsilon\) denominators).

A key structural obstacle for most candidates: many contain \(T*c0*(c1+\epsilon)^3\). Expanding:
\[
T*c0(\epsilon^3 + 3c1\epsilon^2 + 3c1^2\epsilon + c1^3)
\]
GT’s \(T\)-dependent part has only \(\epsilon^3 T\) and \(T\) (constant-in-\(\epsilon\)) terms, **no \(\epsilon^2T\) or \(\epsilon T\)**. Thus, if such a term is present with nonzero coefficient, we must force \(c1=0\) (to kill \(\epsilon^2T,\epsilon T\)) or force \(c0=0\) (to remove it entirely). If \(c1=0\), then \(T*c0*(c1+\epsilon)^3 = T*c0*\epsilon^3\) and cannot supply the needed constant-in-\(\epsilon\) slope term \(-0.3903\,T\); that constant slope must come from an added \(T*c2\) term.

Now check candidates.

1) Has \(T*c0(c1+\epsilon)^3\) plus \(T*c2\) plus \(T*c3\epsilon\) etc and cosine term. To match GT: need no \(T\epsilon\) term ⇒ set \(c3=0\). Need no \(\epsilon^2,\epsilon\) terms ⇒ set \(c4=c5=0\). Need no cosine ⇒ set \(c7=0\). Still left with \(T*c0(c1+\epsilon)^3 + T*c2 + c6\). To avoid \(T\epsilon^2,T\epsilon\) ⇒ set \(c1=0\), giving \(T*c0\epsilon^3 + T*c2 + c6\). But GT also has a pure \(\epsilon^3\) term independent of \(T\); candidate lacks it unless \(c6\) depends on \(\epsilon\) (it doesn’t). So cannot match.

2) Similar; no separate \(T*c2\) constant slope unless embedded; also has cosine. Killing cosine gives \(T*c0(c1+\epsilon)^3 + c2\epsilon^2 + c3\epsilon + c4\). No way to create GT’s \(\epsilon^3 T\) and also \(\epsilon^3\) intercept with correct \(T\)-dependence; also missing \(T\) constant term. No match.

3) Has sine in \(T\). GT is linear in \(T\); a sine term can only be removed by setting its amplitude \(c4=0\). Then reduces to polynomial with \(T*c0(c1+\epsilon)^3 + T*c2 + T*c3\epsilon + c7\epsilon^2 + c8\epsilon + c9\). Must set \(c3=c7=c8=0\), \(c1=0\) to avoid extra \(T\epsilon,T\epsilon^2\). Then \(T*c0\epsilon^3 + T*c2 + c9\). Still no \(\epsilon^3\) intercept term. No match.

4) Has \(\exp(T*c7)\) term; must set \(c5=0\) to remove nonlinearity in \(T\). Then becomes \(T*c0(c1+\epsilon)^3 + c2\epsilon^2 + c3\epsilon + c4\). No \(T\) constant slope term unless via \(c1^3\) but that introduces \(\epsilon^2T,\epsilon T\) unless \(c1=0\). With \(c1=0\) it’s \(T*c0\epsilon^3 + \text{(no }T\text{ constant)}\). No match.

5) Similar; exp term removable, but still cannot generate both \(\epsilon^3\) intercept and correct \(T\)-affine structure. No match.

6) \(T*c0(c1+\epsilon)^3 + c2\epsilon^{c3} + c4\epsilon^2 + c5\epsilon + c6\). No \(T\) constant term; and to avoid \(T\epsilon^2,T\epsilon\) need \(c1=0\). Then \(T*c0\epsilon^3 +\) (terms independent of \(T\)). Could set \(c2\epsilon^{c3}\) to \(\epsilon^3\) by \(c3=3\), but GT’s \(\epsilon^3\) intercept is not just a single coefficient; it is \(4.2558\epsilon^3 - 8.6380*308.8647\,\epsilon^3\) plus also a constant \(+0.3903*308.8647\). Candidate could match the \(\epsilon^3\) intercept with \(c2\) but cannot produce the **constant** intercept term \(+0.3903*308.8647\) simultaneously unless \(c6\) supplies it (it can). However still missing the \(T\) constant slope term \(-0.3903 T\). No match.

7) Contains rational \(1/(c3+\epsilon)\) terms; GT has none. Only removable by setting those coefficients \(c2=c9=0\). Then has \(T*c0\epsilon + T*c1 + T*c4(c5+\epsilon)^{c6} + c7\epsilon + c8\). To get \(\epsilon^3T\) need \((c5+\epsilon)^{c6}\) with \(c6=3\) and \(c5=0\), but then also introduces no extra powers—ok. Yet there is also \(T*c0\epsilon\) which must be zero ⇒ \(c0=0\). Then \(T*c1 + T*c4\epsilon^3 + c7\epsilon + c8\). Must set \(c7=0\). Now we have \(T\) constant and \(T\epsilon^3\) and constant intercept, but **still missing** the \(\epsilon^3\) intercept term. No match.

8) \(T*c0(c1+\epsilon)^3 + c2\epsilon^{c3} + c4\epsilon^3 + c5\epsilon + c6\). No \(T\) constant term; same issue. No match.

9) \(T*c0(c1+\epsilon)^3 + T*c2\epsilon^3 + c3\epsilon^2 + c4\epsilon + c5 + c6\epsilon^3\). To avoid \(T\epsilon^2,T\epsilon\) need \(c1=0\). Then \(T*(c0+c2)\epsilon^3 + c6\epsilon^3 + c5\). Still no \(T\) constant slope term \(-0.3903T\). No match.

10) Has \(T*c0(c1+\epsilon)^3 + T*c2 + T*c3\epsilon + T*c4|\epsilon|^3 + ... + c8|\epsilon|^3\). Using domain \(\epsilon\ge0\), \(|\epsilon|^3=\epsilon^3\). To match GT: set \(c3=0\), \(c5=c6=0\). Need to avoid \(T\epsilon^2,T\epsilon\) from \((c1+\epsilon)^3\) ⇒ set \(c1=0\) or \(c0=0\). If set \(c1=0\), term becomes \(T*c0\epsilon^3\). Then total \(T\)-part is \(T*(c2 + (c0+c4)\epsilon^3)\), which can match GT slope by choosing \(c2=-0.3902956878\) and \(c0+c4=8.6380281543\). Intercept part is \(c7 + c8\epsilon^3\). But GT intercept is \(A + B\epsilon^3\) with a specific constant \(A=0.3902956878*308.8646781\) and specific \(\epsilon^3\) coefficient \(B=4.2558304788 - 8.6380281543*308.8646781\). Candidate can match by setting \(c7=A\), \(c8=B\). This seems promising—however we forgot GT also has the \(+4.2558\epsilon^3\) term; that is included in \(B\epsilon^3\) after rewriting, so OK. Therefore candidate 10 **can** match GT on domain \(\epsilon\ge0\).

11) Same as 10 but without Abs. Even easier: set \(c3=0,c5=c6=0,c1=0\). Choose \(c2=-0.3902956878\), \(c0+c4=8.6380281543\), \(c7=0.3902956878*308.8646781\), \(c8=4.2558304788-8.6380281543*308.8646781\). Exact match. So 11 matches.

12) Similar but power \(Abs(\epsilon)^{c5}\) with shared exponent in both T and non-T terms. Set \(c5=3\) and \(\epsilon\ge0\) so Abs drops. Then same fitting as 10; also must kill extra \(\epsilon^2,\epsilon\) terms by setting \(c6=c7=0\) and \(c1=0,c3=0\). Works. Match.

13) Has \(\exp(c7/T)\) non-affine in \(T\); must set \(c5=0\) to remove. Then no \(T\) constant term; no match.

14-15) Include logs and higher powers; GT has none; only removable by zeroing coefficients, but then structure is \(T*c0\epsilon + T*c1\epsilon^3 + ...\) lacking \(T\) constant slope and/or correct intercept. No match.

16) Has extra \(\epsilon^{c8}\exp(c9/T)\); set \(c7=0\) to remove. Then reduces to candidate 24 type with \(\epsilon^2,\epsilon\) etc; cannot create \(\epsilon^3\) intercept while keeping correct \(T\)-affine slope unless using Abs-power terms like 10-12. No match.

17-18) exp(T*c9) terms; must set their amplitudes 0; then same issue as 24. No match.

With \(c1=0\), slope is \(c2 + c0\epsilon^3\) which can match. Intercept is \(c8 + c4\epsilon^3 + c6\epsilon^2 + c7\epsilon\); set \(c6=c7=0\). Wait: but GT intercept’s \(\epsilon^3\) coefficient is exactly that value, so yes. Therefore 21 also matches (no need for Abs). Good.

**Candidate 80:** `c0*epsilon*exp(T*c1) + c2*(T*c3+c4)**c5 + c6*(T+c4)**c5*Abs(epsilon)**c7`
exp(T*c1) is exponential in T. Can't match polynomial. Set c1=0: `c0*epsilon + c2*(T*c3+c4)**c5 + c6*(T+c4)**c5*Abs(epsilon)**c7`. The power terms (T*c3+c4)**c5 - if c5=1: `c2*(T*c3+c4) + c6*(T+c4)*Abs(epsilon)**c7`. With epsilon≥0, c7=3: `c2*T*c3 + c2*c4 + c6*T*epsilon**3 + c6*c4*epsilon**3 + c0*epsilon`. Set c0=0: `T*(c2*c3 + c6*epsilon**3) + c2*c4 + c6*c4*epsilon**3`. This gives T*c2*c3 + T*c6*epsilon**3 + c2*c4 + c6*c4*epsilon**3. But the epsilon**3 coefficient in the non-T part is c6*c4, and the T*epsilon**3 coefficient is c6. The T coefficient is c2*c3, and constant is c2*c4. So we need c6*c4/c6 = c4 and c2*c4/(c2*c3) = c4/c3. For GT: epsilon**3 coeff ≈ -2663.72, T*epsilon**3 coeff ≈ 8.638, constant ≈ 120.55, T coeff ≈ -0.3903. So c6 = 8.638, c4 = -2663.72/8.638 ≈ -308.4 (close to -308.86). And c2*c3 = -0.3903, c2*c4 = 120.55. So c2 = 120.55/c4 = 120.55/(-308.4) ≈ -0.391, c3 = -0.3903/(-0.391) ≈ 0.998. 

But wait, the GT has c3=c6=308.8647. Let me check: c4 here would need to equal -c3 (from GT) = -308.8647. Then c6*c4 = 8.638*(-308.8647) = -2667.97 but GT epsilon**3 coeff is 4.2558 - 8.638*308.8647 ≈ -2663.71. These don't match exactly because 4.2558 ≠ 0. The issue is that in GT, the epsilon**3 constant term is c0 - c5*c6 = 4.2558 - 8.638*308.865, while in candidate 80 it's c6*c4. And T*epsilon**3 coeff is c6 (candidate) = c5 (GT) = 8.638. And T coeff is c2*c3 (candidate) = -c2 (GT) = -0.3903. And constant is c2*c4 (candidate) = c2*c3 (GT) = 0.3903*308.865 = 120.55.

In candidate 80: constant = c2*c4, T coeff = c2*c3, epsilon**3 coeff = c6*c4, T*epsilon**3 coeff = c6.

So: constant/T_coeff = c4/c3, and epsilon3_coeff/T_epsilon3_coeff = c4.

From GT: constant/T_coeff = 120.55/(-0.3903) = -308.86, and epsilon3_coeff/T_epsilon3_coeff = -2663.71/8.638 = -308.40.

These are NOT equal (-308.86 ≠ -308.40). So the constraint c4 appears in both ratios but they give different values. This means candidate 80 CANNOT match GT exactly because it has a structural constraint (the same c4 appears in both the constant and epsilon**3 terms).

Actually wait, let me reconsider. In GT: c0*epsilon**3 - c2*(T-c3) + epsilon**3*c5*(T-c6) with c3=c6=308.865.

So GT = c0*epsilon**3 - c2*T + c2*c3 + c5*epsilon**3*T - c5*c6*epsilon**3
= T*(c5*epsilon**3 - c2) + (c0 - c5*c6)*epsilon**3 + c2*c3

With c3=c6: constant = c2*c3, T coeff = -c2, epsilon**3 coeff = c0 - c5*c3, T*epsilon**3 coeff = c5.

For candidate 80 (with c1=0, c0_cand=0, c5_cand=1, c3_cand set, c7=3):
constant = c2*c4, T coeff = c2*c3_cand, epsilon**3 coeff = c6_cand*c4, T*epsilon**3 coeff = c6_cand.

Matching: c6_cand = c5_GT = 8.638, c2_cand*c3_cand = -c2_GT = -0.3903, c2_cand*c4_cand = c2_GT*c3_GT = 120.55, c6_cand*c4_cand = c0_GT - c5_GT*c3_GT.

From the last: c4_cand = (c0_GT - c5_GT*c3_GT)/c6_cand = (4.2558 - 8.638*308.865)/8.638 = (4.2558 - 2667.97)/8.638 = -2663.71/8.638 ≈ -308.37.

From c2_cand*c4_cand = 120.55: c2_cand = 120.55/(-308.37) ≈ -0.3911.
From c2_cand*c3_cand = -0.3903: c3_cand = -0.3903/(-0.3911) ≈ 0.998.

But we also need c4_cand to satisfy: c4_cand = c2_GT*c3_GT/c2_cand = 120.55/(-0.3911) = -308.24.

But we got c4_cand ≈ -308.37 from the other equation. These are different! So there's an inconsistency. The candidate has 4 unknowns but 4 equations, and they're over-determined due to the structural constraint. [NO MATCH]
